Ladz, this ainâ€™t no conspiracy theory. Hear me out. These 12 clubs have created this super league as a leverage in negotiations with their respective local league. You see, a couple of years back, the big teams that dominated their local leagues made quite a large percentage of their leagueâ€™s TV rights. This was based on the popularity of each match being watched on TV. This led to a wider â€˜club worthâ€™ gap between clubs in the same league and results like Barcelona 7-1. And these big clubs basically dominated. But recently, the leagues have caught up on this and begun distributing the money almost evenly to the clubs in the league. Which is giving less popular clubs more money and so better transfers, and resources. So the big clubs are not happy about this, because A they arenâ€™t getting as much % money as they used to and B, because these less popular teams are now better equipped and put up tougher games against the big clubs. Therefore, the big clubs have created this super league as a negotiating tool to allow for greater percentage profits from their respective leagues. I honestly think that this super league wonâ€™t happen as the repercussions on the clubs is too big, but it will help them secure a bigger share of the TV rights $ in their league.

Sorry this was inevitable and with the pandemic was  accelerated.  Uefa can try to claim â€œinnocenceâ€ that theyâ€™re not involved. But they have been looking at this proposal for years and are very much involved...  the reality is as Football is the worlds most popular sport the CL should attract more revenues than the NFL and unfortunately they do not... looking at the ratings they have established that when the elite clubs play each other viewings go through the roof, however for the smaller games which we see during the group stages  it just doesnâ€™t happen.   The tipping point for clubs particularly the premiership clubs is the fact that the broadcasting revenue is not distributed in the same manner as it is in Spain where the likes of Liverpool who with the EPL and the CL within 2 seasons still cant compete with Barcelona and Madrid in the transfer market...  The reason being the premiership distributes the TV money in a way that basically mean the Big 4 are subsidizing the league.. domestically it is estimated the 80% of the uk fanatic and casual football fanbase support/ follow Utd, Liverpool, Arsenal and Tottenham.. and itâ€™s those who buy the subscriptions... this is even proven in the ratings where they go through the roof when these clubs play each other...with the global market Tottenham are replaced by Chelsea following their recent success and foreign imports during the mid to late 90s. What is frustrating the owners is that domestic revenue has 50% of the total value split evenly among the the 20 clubs before a ball is kicked. 25% is issued on league placement and the other 25% is issued based on appearances on the TV... The foreign broadcasting revenues 100% is distributed evenly amongst all 20 clubs...  This is not meritocracy as we keep hearing for those who oppose the super league.. this is football socialism where 16 clubs benefit from the global fan based of Utd, Liverpool and Arsenal who should be competing on budgets that eclipse Barcelona and Real Madrid..   This is made worse when the international broadcasting revenue for Laliga is distributed based on club buy outs meaning Barca and Real Madrid secure a substantial amount of revenues as a result..  To show how ridiculous it is - before the recent TV deal came in for the premiership which was the season Aston Villa got relegated. Their bottom placed finish secured earnings considerably more than Bayern Munich and PSG of whom competed in the CL and won all their domestic titles..  So again the arguments being held so regarding meritocracy ... how is it that a club finishing bottom and getting relegated can earn more prize money than clubs who win their respective league and Cup competitions? (With a global fan base I may add)..   Itâ€™s like anything in life you donâ€™t get the rewards you feel you deserve ... youâ€™ll seek out an opportunity where you will get a better deal... this proposal was inevitable...

A football league from which its founding members can never be relegated; the ultimate closed shop.  But these are currently the elite clubs of Europe and likely to remain so, able to attract the world's top players with vast salaries and a guaranteed promise of football every week against Europe's ultimate teams.  Threats of relegation, point deductions, loss of titles or a ban on players competing at international level all ring hollow. UEFA, FIFA and the Premier League are utterly impotent. These clubs' owners care nothing for history or titles, only money. The Premier League without the big six, a World Cup bereft of the very best, or Champions League devoid of the top clubs are all finished.  Capitalism at its worst and the ultimate example of what can happen when businessmen with zero interest in football are allowed free rein to purchase the world's top clubs.

As much as I am sad to see this, what the Super League is trying to do is copy the financial success model of the NBA and F1. Sure, there are other basketball or racing series, but the one people want to watch are the elite competitions like NBA, or F1. On the business side, every major broadcast companies would want to sign the rights to play the Super League matches, which will result in big revenue. This will then attract bigger sponsor payouts. So, bigger revenue means higher salary wages, which then attracts the best players to play. FIFA and UEFA can ban these players from the World Cup or Euros all they want, but at the end of the day players play for the paycheck. In the future, kids around the world will grow up and dream of playing in the Super League. International competitions will be a non factor as the glamour and the glitz of fame and fortune can only come from playing in the Super League. As for the grassroots to find future talents, these elite clubs will be able to set up academies and youth competitions throughout the world to ensure the best talents only play in the Super League.
